## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt in a chemical reaction system. The rate law typically depends on concentration A (through mass-action kinetics) and possibly explicitly on time t (through coupled species, external forcing, or integrated forms).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (first-order reaction rate law)
- Second-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (second-order reaction in single species)
- nth-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate expression)
- Mixed order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (combined first and second order kinetics)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reaction with equilibrium)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalytic reaction)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate with time-varying external influence)
- Coupled pseudo-rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (implicit dependence on another species decaying exponentially)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (substrate inhibition)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant source/sink)
- Competitive pathway: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (c1 + A) (second-order with saturation)
- Oscillatory forcing: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (periodic external driving of reaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Mass-action kinetics: rate proportional to product of reactant concentrations raised to stoichiometric powers â†’ dA_dt = c * A**n
- Enzyme saturation: when rate plateaus at high concentration, use rational forms A/(K+A) rather than pure power laws
- Reversible reactions approaching equilibrium: rate expression should vanish at equilibrium concentration â†’ terms like c0*(A - A_eq)
- Implicit coupled species: if another species B follows B(t) = B0*exp(-k*t), its effect appears as explicit time dependence in A's rate law
- Conservation laws: in closed systems, total concentration is conserved, so (c1 - A) terms appear representing complementary species
- Negative rates for consumption: dA_dt should be negative when A is being consumed, constraining sign of leading coefficient
- Cooperative kinetics: Hill-type nonlinearity A**n/(K**n + A**n) indicates cooperative binding or multi-step activation
- Sequential mechanism signatures: products of exponentials in time exp(c1*t) - exp(c2*t) indicate intermediate species in series reactions
